The analysis will confirm that the bridge can safely transfer the combined load of the SPMT and cargo to the vessel deck without exceeding allowable stress or deflection limits.\n\nBow Deck Strength Calculation\nAssessment of the LCT bow deck structure to ensure it can sustain the applied wheel loads from the SPMT during the loading and offloading operations. The calculation will determine load distribution and confirm compliance with the vessel's allowable deck loading capacity.\n\nIntact Stability check during the loading sequence\nEvaluation of the vessel's intact stability throughout the loadout operation, from the initial ballasting condition to final loading. The analysis will verify that the vessel remains within acceptable stability criteria and maintains adequate trim and heel at all stages of the operation.\n\nFollowing information would be required to complete this task\n\n- Ballast tank arrangement and capacity plan.\n- Sequence of loading (step-by-step movement of SPMT and cargo).\n\nKindly note that, as per our previous discussion regarding the job scope of the subject vessel, our understanding was to perform an intact stability check for the loading conditions corresponding to each loadout sequence provided by your team.\n\nTo facilitate this, we were requesting you to share the complete loading sequence for the barge, including the load on the barge and the amount of ballast at each step.\n\nThe loads previous have been also approximately estimated from our end to carry out the Strength check of the steel bridge and the bow deck structure but for loadout this needs to be recalculated more accurately as this is related to the vessel stability.\n\nThe loadout calculation is a detailed engineering assessment carried out to ensure the safe and controlled transfer of the cargo (transformer) from the shore/jetty onto the LCT vessel using SPMT.\nThis analysis covers the following aspects:\n\nDetermination of load distribution and reactions on the jetty, steel bridge, and vessel deck during each stage of the SPMT movement.\nEvaluation of the vessel's intact stability and trim/heel conditions throughout the loading sequence.\nCalculation of hydrostatic parameters and verification against applicable stability criteria (e.g., GM, righting arm curve, and permissible heel angles).\nAssessment of the required ballast adjustments at each stage to maintain safe stability and acceptable draft/trim levels. If not ballasting can be done during loading due to any reason then we will have to study what is the draft that needs to be maintained throughout this loading operation etc.\nIdentification of any critical stages where corrective ballasting or operational control is required.\n\nAbove is a brief description for your info.\n\nIn case that our scope is extended to include preparation of the complete loadout sequence, we will need to develop the detailed loading steps, load transfer stages, and ballasting plan from the basics.\n\nThis will involve additional engineering effort for:\n\n- Developing the full loadout plan and sequence,\n- Performing detailed static and stability calculations for each stage, and\n- Preparing the supporting documentation and reports.\n\nAs informed, this additional scope will have time and cost implications, and is expected to require approximately 7–10 working days to complete, subject to receipt of all required data.\n\nPlease review and confirm your intention for us to proceed with this additional task, so that we can update our proposal and schedule accordingly.\n\nThanks and Best Regards,\nFrom Aries Marine, UAE\nSonal Singh"

#### Msg 25 — Sonal Singh @ 2025-10-24 09:22 +04:00 {#msg-25}
| Key | Value |
|---|---|
| From | Sonal Singh <d***@ariesofs.ae> |
| To | Haitham Madaneya |
| Cc | Multiple |
| Subject | RE: [HVDC] - AGI Transformers Transportation - Vessel Stability and Deck Strength / LCT Bushra DU5025 |

```text
Dear Mr. Haitham,

Good day!

As discussed, sending you description of the following scopes which are part of our current scope of work

Strength check of the steel bridge
Verification of the structural adequacy of the temporary steel bridge (or link span) that will connect the jetty and the LCT during the loadout operation. The analysis will confirm that the bridge can safely transfer the combined load of the SPMT and cargo to the vessel deck without exceeding allowable stress or deflection limits.

Bow Deck Strength Calculation
Assessment of the LCT bow deck structure to ensure it can sustain the applied wheel loads from the SPMT during the loading and offloading operations. The calculation will determine load distribution and confirm compliance with the vessel's allowable deck loading capacity.

Intact Stability check during the loading sequence
Evaluation of the vessel's intact stability throughout the loadout operation, from the initial ballasting condition to final loading. The analysis will verify that the vessel remains within acceptable stability criteria and maintains adequate trim and heel at all stages of the operation.

Following information would be required to complete this task

- Ballast tank arrangement and capacity plan.
- Sequence of loading (step-by-step movement of SPMT and cargo).

Kindly note that, as per our previous discussion regarding the job scope of the subject vessel, our understanding was to perform an intact stability check for the loading conditions corresponding to each loadout sequence provided by your team.

To facilitate this, we were requesting you to share the complete loading sequence for the barge, including the load on the barge and the amount of ballast at each step.

The loads previous have been also approximately estimated from our end to carry out the Strength check of the steel bridge and the bow deck structure but for loadout this needs to be recalculated more accurately as this is related to the vessel stability.

The loadout calculation is a detailed engineering assessment carried out to ensure the safe and controlled transfer of the cargo (transformer) from the shore/jetty onto the LCT vessel using SPMT.
This analysis covers the following aspects:

Determination of load distribution and reactions on the jetty, steel bridge, and vessel deck during each stage of the SPMT movement.
Evaluation of the vessel's intact stability and trim/heel conditions throughout the loading sequence.
Calculation of hydrostatic parameters and verification against applicable stability criteria (e.g., GM, righting arm curve, and permissible heel angles).
Assessment of the required ballast adjustments at each stage to maintain safe stability and acceptable draft/trim levels. If not ballasting can be done during loading due to any reason then we will have to study what is the draft that needs to be maintained throughout this loading operation etc.
Identification of any critical stages where corrective ballasting or operational control is required.

Above is a brief description for your info.

In case that our scope is extended to include preparation of the complete loadout sequence, we will need to develop the detailed loading steps, load transfer stages, and ballasting plan from the basics.

This will involve additional engineering effort for:

- Developing the full loadout plan and sequence,
- Performing detailed static and stability calculations for each stage, and
- Preparing the supporting documentation and reports.

As informed, this additional scope will have time and cost implications, and is expected to require approximately 7–10 working days to complete, subject to receipt of all required data.

Please review and confirm your intention for us to proceed with this additional task, so that we can update our proposal and schedule accordingly.

Thanks and Best Regards,
From Aries Marine, UAE
Sonal Singh
```

```text
Dear Capt. Joey and Yulia,

We have finalized the simulation based on the corrected cargo weight (280t) and the DAS Method (Pre-ballasting).

[Conclusion] The operation is confirmed SAFE and FEASIBLE. We request your final approval to mobilize.

1. Key Updates & Ballast Plan
• Cargo Weight: Corrected to 280.00 tons (TR Unit 217t + SPMT/Acc 63t).
• Ballast: Optimized to 200.00 tons (Reduced from initial estimate due to lighter cargo).
• Method: Shore Water Supply will be used to bypass onboard pump limits.
• Tank Verification: We will utilize Aft Tanks (FWB1/2). As per Tank Plan 757 TCP, these are confirmed at Frame 48–65 (Aft).

2. Stability Verification (Stage 6A - Critical)
• Trim: Perfect Even Keel (-0.10 m) at the moment of ramp entry.
• Fwd Draft: 2.77 m (Safe). This prevents deck submergence with ample freeboard (+0.88 m).
• Note: The high stern trim (+1.49m) during the preparation phase is an intentional counter-weight setup to prevent bow diving.

3. Operational Requirements
• Tugboat: Continuous pushing is required during Roll-on for station keeping.
• Depth Check: Please ensure >4.00 m depth clearance at the stern during the pre-ballasting phase.

Best regards,
```

```text
•	A minimum draft of 2.7 m, especially at the aft, must be maintained to ensure effective propeller operation in case of emergency.
```

```text
- Reaction of LCT when the load is transferred from jetty to LCT Bushra. Specifically, we'd like to know the FWD and AFT draft data for each stage, so that our Engineering team would be able to do minimum tide checking.
```

```text
GBP of Jetty and calculations related to it doesn’t fall within our Scope.

25.2t – Load per axle
1.4m – length of axle 
3.650m – width of acting area
5.11sq.m – area
4.93t – GBP per sq.m.


Hope above is sufficient from our side.

ADNOC Classification: Internal
 
Dear Mr. Jeong,
 
As per latest update, understand that Loading is planned for 26-Jan, so I plan to bring Bushra to Mina Zayed by 25th evening or 26th early morning.
 
Kind reminder to arrange corner jetty to be able to utilize Bushra’s mooring ropes (when ramp is on the jetty, there should be a jetty wall alongside the vessel too / corner jetty), so we could avoid anchored winches on the jetty.
 
Further to our discussion yesterday, please double check tide situation with 3rd party who made calculations of ballasting steps. My concern for upcoming first loading is that we will be wating for tide for quite a long time after first part of load come on to deck. The whole trailer will be hanging on linkspan for very long time till tide helps to equalize the levels of deck and jetty. This long time hanging on linkspan is very dangerous and exposing us to various uncontrollable risks (vessel movement in harbour creating waives, wind change, etc). 
Please double check with 3rd party if we are going to pump out the water or transfer the water from fwd to aft?

Dear   @차민규,
 
Good noon! With reference to the below email, please be advised that land permits are also required for SPMT operations, and the approval process typically takes approximately 2–3 working days. As the weekend falls within this period, the approvals may take additional time.
 
Furthermore, a pre-arrival meeting should be arranged prior to the vessel’s arrival for operations planning with the port authorities. We will keep you informed once the meeting is finalized. In the meantime, please find below the relevant documents for your perusal regarding cargo loading/offloading operations.
```
